  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_86c94330-0dd2-47b0-909d-1920bbb6c45e'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736349817" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736349817?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=books-i-enjoyed-reading">books-i-enjoyed-reading</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736349817" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12604788798059415027">Dayum….dayum….dayuummm<br/>Ugh I’m so mad and disappointed……no not with the book but because of the “mistakes” the characters did in this book. But it was an awesome read as usual. <br/><br/>***********HUGE SPOILERS AHEAD*********<br/><br/>Book 7<br/><br/>This book was not packed with loads of action like the last book, but this book is vital for understanding the prophecy! I mean, even though this book is not action packed …it was still a page turner, considering that you learn a LOT of things about Mr.Tiny, the prophecy, the ro</span>
  <span id="freeText12604788798059415027" style="display:none">Dayum….dayum….dayuummm<br />Ugh I’m so mad and disappointed……no not with the book but because of the “mistakes” the characters did in this book. But it was an awesome read as usual. <br /><br />***********HUGE SPOILERS AHEAD*********<br /><br />Book 7<br /><br />This book was not packed with loads of action like the last book, but this book is vital for understanding the prophecy! I mean, even though this book is not action packed …it was still a page turner, considering that you learn a LOT of things about Mr.Tiny, the prophecy, the role of future seers and many more. So I enjoyed this book very much. In fact, I finished this book very fast. It was so engaging, I was so intrigued with Lady Evanna and Vancha. <br />I love how we get to meet all the circus mates from the first book, you get to see just how much inner clashing and emotional turmoil Darren felt when he saw Evra’s children and wife. I pity Darren for that, because of his slow aging and unable to bear children. Darren’s rapid caveman hairy growth was hilarious. OMG he is hairy all over LOL. It was great to see how the process works on a half vampire. <br />Spoilers ahead –if you read this review without reading the book first…..not my problem<br />In the aftermath after the battle with vampaneze, they should have listen and burn into their memory of Evanna’s most vital clue.<br /> <br /><i>“If you have something that is precious, and others are looking for it. Where is the best place to hide it?” People searching or hunting, rarely find what they seek if it is placed directly before them, it’s common to overlook that which is most obvious.</i><br /><br />This clue is more important than anything, it was not something they should have thought about one time and forget about it. Every decision they make should have been considered with the clue given by Evanna. <br /><br />Even before Evanna gave that clue, I was wondering why during the fight, why did the lean vampaneze was even bothered to help an injured servant, he is not even his friend or a full blooded vampaneze, but he went so much as to protect him, stop and grab him when he was axed in the back and flit with a servant, risking his life. Tiny clues like this were missed by all 4 of them including the smart Harkat. <br /><br />Book 8 <br />This book is what I was kind of anticipating, hehe because I have the bad habit of always googling for Darren Shan Saga’s Wikipedia. So I already knew by accident of some of the important things that is about to happen, although I was lucky enough not to know in which book it would take place. Having said that, I was very delighted that Darren had liked a black girl called Debbie back in the third book, I was really hoping she would appearance in latter book, which is how I knew she will come back in this book. HEHEHEH<br /><br />I loved how Darren and Debbie’s meeting turned out. It was cute, happy and funny at the same time. Debbie was still the same kid inside but now a 25 year old English teacher in school. It was amazing, Darren is so giddy with lovey dovey feeling LOL. But to be honest, I read many negative remarks as to why Debbie rejected Darren’s request to start a romantic affair. I support Debbie, I mean it is weird to have a 14 year old kid as your boyfriend when you are 25 years old and worse being his English teacher in school, it does not matter if she believed Darren’s slow aging illness, it just too weird and confusing for her, she needs time. So I don’t know why people are bitching about her. Not everyone can simply fall in love quickly, Debbie obviously cares about Darren but she needs time. <br /><br /> At one point I was suspicious of Debbie, because you don’t know who is Vampets anymore. But the moment Steve made appearance, I knew something was really up and I knew Steve is no ordinary vampire hunter. Nor did I believe his revelation that he is not evil. There are a few tiny clues about Steve that should have been picked up by Darren, but he chose not to. I was just as suspicious of Steve as Harkat was, I rolled my eyes when Darren invited him back to his apartment, simply buying everything he is saying without second guessing anything. At that time I seriously wanted to knock some sense in Darren. <br /><br />I was angry that Darren , he did not even think hummm….too many coincidence…meeting Debbie and Steve in Crepsley’s brith city that has series of murders. Gosh how did any of them not see that coming. As much as I love that Debbie is brave and chose to fight along side the others, I also cannot help but think Gurl, you are just going to get caught and used as bait ……maybe not join them in a battle that you have no experience in fighting. Sigh……go figure!!!<br /><br />Book 9<br />This book was by far the best, a lot of action and drama. I loved it !!<br />So much was going on in this book, I like that the author had used this book to bring Darren Shan into the normal world we human lived in, I like how they were running not only from Vampet, vampaneze and police but also from the angry crazy human mob. It was like a reality check !! A strong vampire you maybe but you can’t fight them all. Kekekek <br /><br />Oh I wanted to much to smack that smart mouth Steve in head. Sigh if only they had seen the tiny but obvious clues about him !!!! I was so angry when they did not see why the vampaneze would even remotely worry about saving half blooded Steve, and try to keep making deals to spare him. Like when Steve said he is only doing it for revenge, but why would they even bother with him if he got caught ! The clue was right there !!! Nobody saw it coming. <br /><br />Debbie had said something that would have been a dynamic clue <i>“Don’t trust them, They let Steve and RV do as they please. They even take orders from them “</i> . If anyone had heard that, They would have wondered why would anyone listen to half blooded vampaneze and an idiot blade vampaneze over their Lord!!! There right there, they should have wondered, if their enemy prophecy was said only their Lord can defeat the choosen 3, why did Steve had to fight with Harse and Lord. It made no sense unless Steve is not who he claims to be. Why would a half blooded guy be allowed to fight with the lord !! There was all the clue right there, but nobody had the time to stop and think about it. You know as evil as the Vampaneze is, you can’t help but think they are good in their game !! They know all the good tricks!!<br /><br />Like I said before, I always knew Mr. Crepsley was going to die, but I did not know in which book, so I guess when the time came, I knew this was it. It was devastating because he died in vain !!! Steve still won over him in the end. Steve’s revelation at the end did not surprise me at all for I already knew who he was!. But it was a sad thing through and through !!<br /><br />Few things that got me:-<br />Harkat's height is about 4 feet, but I'm curious about some of his fighting posture because sometimes he sound like he is as tall as Darren<br />How is he even able to put his arm around Debbie, when she is much taller than Darren. <br />Steve said "You mean the dark-skinned lady" rather than simply saying “ black lady”</span>
  <a data-text-id="12604788798059415027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1552989583069246326">Okay, so....these books are getting very stupid and I hate it.<br/>I mean Darren was sort of oblivious up until now but in here he's just a whole ass idiot, trusts people for no reason and decides to do the worst things. However, that's not even the worst thing!<br/><br/>What the actual thing was that whole thing with Debbie ?? I know that in vampire and human romances there's always the argument of "he's immortal and doesn't look like his age" but uh, he looks like he's fifteen and acts like he's twelve so th</span>
  <span id="freeText1552989583069246326" style="display:none">Okay, so....these books are getting very stupid and I hate it.<br />I mean Darren was sort of oblivious up until now but in here he's just a whole ass idiot, trusts people for no reason and decides to do the worst things. However, that's not even the worst thing!<br /><br />What the actual thing was that whole thing with Debbie ?? I know that in vampire and human romances there's always the argument of "he's immortal and doesn't look like his age" but uh, he looks like he's fifteen and acts like he's twelve so there's nothing for Debbie to like there. I'm usually one to say that vampires and other immortal beings can have romances with humans as long as the human is not a minor but here there's just a line that I can't define but bothers me anyway. <br /><br />Larten was especially dumb too, which I'm highly disappointed about.<br />The whole part where Darren was sent to school for like half a chapter and then chased by the police....what the actual fuck<br /><br />Anyway, I hated this lmao, I will finish the three books left because I got this far, goddammit I won't give up!<br /><br />PS: I totally predicted that Mr Shan would kill off Larten because why the fuck not, he has no shame at this point. I barely even want to read the rest good God.</span>

The twist at the end...how there was hope and then it was swept from under my feet...the ending has left me an emotional wreck. <br/><br/>But don't let that deter you, this trilogy has been the best so far of this series, and I can't wait to read the final trilogy. </span>

  <span id="freeText12126573681547375682" style="display:none">I first read the Saga of Darren Shan when I started year 7, I found the books in the corner of the school library just begging to be read. My friend recommended them so I didn't think twice about it, I picked the books up and read the entire series within a week. Darren is such a good character to be the narrator of the story. Of course this is a vampire book, and it follows vampires (half and full vampires) and another species of vampire called the vampaneze (half and full). The vampires are the 'good guys' if you like and they only take a little blood from their victim (they can survive off animal blood but to have their full strength they need human blood) whereas the vampaneze are the 'bad guys' who drain their victims of blood; they have red eyes, extremely sharp nails, and a purple hue to their skin. Neither of these species have fangs contrary to the normal vision of vampires. </span>

<div id="review_1754725989" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1754725989" />
    <a title="Mothwing" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2268636-mothwing"><img alt="Mothwing" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312073278p2/2268636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1754725989?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mothwing" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mothwing" href="/user/show/2268636-mothwing">Mothwing</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2268636-mothwing?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2268636-mothwing?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2268636-mothwing?shelf=abuse-as-backstory">abuse-as-backstory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2268636-mothwing?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2268636-mothwing?shelf=violence">violence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2268636-mothwing?shelf=manly-men">manly-men</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1754725989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14014254695202555287">Torture is cool, there are people who are pure evil, and what the hell is the age group that these books are geared towards? I have always been baffled by the surprising level of senseless violence in them, but confronting reluctant readers who love action-packed books which are violent and have high stakes (and this is kind of who I'm guessing they're for?) that also condone torture and have the mentor figure saying that there are people who have been born evil just makes it worse. Entertaining</span>
  <span id="freeText14014254695202555287" style="display:none">Torture is cool, there are people who are pure evil, and what the hell is the age group that these books are geared towards? I have always been baffled by the surprising level of senseless violence in them, but confronting reluctant readers who love action-packed books which are violent and have high stakes (and this is kind of who I'm guessing they're for?) that also condone torture and have the mentor figure saying that there are people who have been born evil just makes it worse. Entertaining, yes, and I am going to read the last instalment of this series, but I will definitely NOT add them to our classroom library after all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14014254695202555287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HOdQLX+4saP/bsyssArzZncYSQQxgL1NdNgW8kdNMDUE83XjKw6VUpHoqqDqmv+aR9UNTSoIiMwE2aAUfxwY4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QsWN65IXwc/u1QdTYTGwdlhrbpOhCnB+8GMXpXsNTmda0aglxqHlPoBTYV87obyKaKYq2rqCRf+AYqFDQ1xmsQ==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4145118088856056799">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan' rel='nofollow noopener'>D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br/><br/>Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak</span>
  <span id="freeText4145118088856056799" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>
